Talaq — Divorce

6 min
Immediate and Time-Added Divorce Are Mutually Exclusive
Explains the incompatibility of immediate and time-added divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle regarding immediate and time-added divorce and apply it to scenarios with past, present, and future time references.

Core Idea
Immediate divorce and time-added divorce are mutually exclusive in Hanafi law.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a key principle: the categories of immediate (munajjiz) and added (mudaf) divorce cannot mix. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly applying divorce pronouncements that mention time. The author uses logical reasoning (dalil aqli) to demonstrate that adding a future time defers the divorce, while past or present references are ignored.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Categories
Recognize that divorce can be immediate (munajjiz) or added to a future time (mudaf). The two are opposites.
2
Apply the Place–Time Distinction
Note that place references do not restrict divorce, but time references do—at least for the future.
Place is irrelevant because divorce is not location-specific.
3
Analyze the Three Time Scenarios
Examine past, present, and future time references. Past and present lead to immediate divorce; future defers the divorce.
Past is treated as futile; present is effectively immediate; future is honored.
4
State the Ruling
Formulate the rule: a divorce with a future time reference takes effect at that time; with past or present, it takes effect immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان
(۵۶) إِنَّ الْمُنَجِّزَ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْإِضَافَةَ وَكَذَا الْمُضَافُ لَا يَتَجَنَّزُ .
ترجمہ: فی الحال واقع ہونے والی طلاق اضافت کا احتمال نہیں رکھتی اور مضاف شدہ فی الحال واقع نہیں ہوسکتی۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ طلاق تجیزی یعنی مطلق طلاق کسی زمانہ کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہو سکتی اور اسی طرح جو طلاق منسوب الی الزمان ہو وہ طلاق تجیزی نہیں ہوسکتی، گویا کہ طلاق تنجیزی اور طلاق منسوب الی الزمان دونوں متضاد چیز میں ہیں ایک ساتھ جمع نہیں ہوسکتیں۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے کہا أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ الْيَوْمَ بِأَنْ قَالَ لِامْرَأَتِهِ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ فِى الدَّارِ أَوْ فِى مَكَّةَ وَقَعَ الطَّلَاقُ وَإِنْ لَمْ تَكُنِ الْمَرْأَةُ فِي الدَّارِ وَلَا فِي مَكَّةَ لأَنَّ الطَّلَاقَ لَا يَخْتَصُّ بِمَكَان دُونَ مَكَان فَإِذَا وَقَعَ فِي مَكَانٍ وَقَعَ فِي الْأَمَاكِنِ كُلِّهَا، وَإِنْ دَخَلَتْ عَلَى الزَّمَانِ فَإِنْ كَانَ مَاضِيًا يَقَعُ الطَّلَاقُ فِي الْحَالِ نَحْوُ أَنْ يَقُولَ أَنْتِ ظَالِقٌ فِي الْأَمْسِ أَوْ فِي الْعَامِ الْمَاضِي لِأَنَّ إِنْشَاء الطَّلَاقِ فِى الزَّمَانِ الْمَاضِي لَا يُتَصَوَّرُ فَيُجْعَلُ إِخْبَارًا أَوْ تَلْغُو الْإِضَافَةُ إِلَى الْمَاضِي وَيَبْقَى قَوْلُهُ أَنْتِ ظَالِقٌ فَيَقَعُ فِي الْحَالِ وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا كَانَ حَاضِرًا بِأَنْ قَالَ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ فِي هَذَا الْوَقْتِ أَوْ فِي هَذِهِ السَّاعَةِ يَقَعُ فِي الْحَالِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مُسْتَقَبَّلًا لَا يَقَعُ حَتَّى يَأْتِيَ بِأَنْ قَالَ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ فِى غَدٍ أَوْ فِى الشَّهْرِ الْآتِى لِأَنَّ الطَّلَاقَ يَحْتَمِلُ الاخْتِصَاصَ بِوَقْتِ دُونَ وَقْتِ فَإِذَا جُعِلَ الْغَدُ ظَرْفًا لَهُ لَا يَقَعُ قَبْلَهُ.
بدائع الصنائع: كتاب الأيمان، فصل فى شرائط ركن الیمین، ج ۳ ص ۲۵، ط: دار الكتب العلمية
الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب إيقاع الطلاق، ج ۲ ص ۳۸۲، ط: رحمانیه
Chapter on Adding Divorce to Time
(56) Indeed, the immediate divorce does not admit addition, and likewise the added divorce cannot be immediate.
Translation: The divorce that occurs immediately does not have the probability of addition, and the added divorce cannot occur immediately.
Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that immediate divorce (talaq tanzizi) i.e. absolute divorce cannot be attributed to a time, and similarly the divorce that is attributed to time cannot be immediate. That is, immediate divorce and time-attributed divorce are two contradictory things that cannot be combined.
The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if someone said 'You are divorced today', then if he said to his wife 'You are divorced in the house or in Mecca', the divorce occurs even if the wife is not in the house or in Mecca, because divorce is not specific to one place over another, so when it occurs in one place, it occurs in all places. And if it enters upon time, then if it is past, the divorce occurs immediately, like if he says 'You are divorced yesterday' or 'in the past year', because initiating divorce in past time is inconceivable, so it is considered a report or the addition to the past becomes futile, and his statement 'you are divorced' remains, so it occurs immediately. Similarly, if it is present, like if he says 'You are divorced in this time' or 'in this hour', it occurs immediately. And if it is future, it does not occur until that time comes, like if he says 'You are divorced tomorrow' or 'next month', because divorce can be specific to one time over another, so when 'tomorrow' is made a container for it, it does not occur before.
Badai' al-Sanai': Kitab al-Ayman, Fasl fi Shara'it Rukn al-Yamin, vol. 3 p. 25, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah.
Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Talaq, Bab Iqa' al-Talaq, vol. 2 p. 382, Rahmaniyyah.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage explains the third principle: 'The immediate divorce cannot be added to time, and the added divorce cannot be immediate.' The author clarifies that these two types of divorce are mutually exclusive. If a man says 'You are divorced yesterday', the divorce takes effect immediately because initiating divorce in the past is impossible, so the time reference is ignored and it becomes an immediate divorce. If he says 'You are divorced tomorrow', it does not occur until tomorrow. The Arabic quote from Badai' al-Sanai' provides detailed examples: for past and present time references, divorce occurs immediately; for future, it is delayed. The Hanafi position distinguishes between place and time: place specification is ignored, but time specification (future) is effective.

Key Terms
منجز (munajjiz): Immediate; a divorce that takes effect at the moment of utterance without any condition or delay.
مضاف (mudaf): Added; a divorce that is attributed to a specific future time and does not take effect until that time arrives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says to his wife 'You are divorced tomorrow' (future). When does the divorce occur according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Immediately
B) At the beginning of the next day
C) Only after one month
D) It does not occur because divorce cannot be added to future time

Key Takeaway
Immediate and time-added divorce are mutually exclusive; future time references defer the divorce while past references are ignored and the divorce is immediate.

Immediate vs Deferred Divorce: The Principle of Tanzīz and Iḍāfah
Ruling principle with examples and case of conflicting time expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tanzīz and iḍāfah to determine when a divorce takes effect when a time condition is mentioned, including cases of conflicting time expressions.

Core Idea
An immediate divorce cannot be added to a future time; a deferred divorce cannot be immediate.

In Hanafi divorce law, the timing of the pronouncement is critical. This lesson explores the principle that an immediate divorce (tanzīz) and a time-attached divorce (iḍāfah) are mutually exclusive. Understanding this principle allows you to correctly determine when a divorce occurs in various scenarios involving time and location references.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the pronouncement
Determine if the husband's statement is immediate (al-munajjiz) or includes a time reference (al-muḍāf). An immediate divorce is one pronounced without any time condition, while a deferred divorce is attached to a future time.
If the statement includes a time phrase like 'tomorrow' or 'next month', it is likely a deferred divorce.
2
Classify the time reference
If a time is mentioned, classify it as past, present, or future. Past (e.g., 'yesterday') and present (e.g., 'today') are treated as immediate. Future (e.g., 'tomorrow') defers the divorce until that time arrives.
In Hanafi law, 'today' is considered present and immediate, not a deferred time.
3
Apply the principle of tanzīz and iḍāfah
For past/present time references, the divorce is immediate because initiating a divorce in past/present time is considered immediate. For future time references, the divorce does not take effect until that time arrives, as the time is a container for the divorce.
This is based on the principle that an immediate divorce cannot be added to a future time, and a deferred divorce cannot be immediate.
4
Handle conflicting time expressions
If the husband mentions two different times (e.g., 'today, tomorrow'), the first word governs. If 'today' comes first, the divorce is immediate and the second time is void. If 'tomorrow' comes first, the divorce is deferred to tomorrow and the 'today' is void.
This is because the first word determines the nature of the divorce, and the contradictory second word is ignored to avoid inconsistency.
5
Distinguish from location references
Unlike time, divorce is not location-specific. If a husband says 'you are divorced in the house' or 'in Mecca', the divorce occurs immediately regardless of whether the wife is there, because the condition does not restrict the divorce to that place.
Location conditions are treated as redundant in Hanafi law, whereas time conditions are effective.

فصل في إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان (۵۶) إِنَّ الْمُنَجِّزَ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْإِضَافَةَ وَكَذَا الْمُضَافُ لَا يَتَنَجَّزُ . ترجمہ: فی الحال واقع ہونے والی طلاق اضافت کا احتمال نہیں رکھتی اور مضاف شدہ فی الحال واقع نہیں ہوسکتی۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ طلاق تجیزی یعنی مطلق طلاق کسی زمانہ کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہو سکتی اور اسی طرح جو طلاق منسوب الی الزمان ہو وہ طلاق تجیزی نہیں ہوسکتی، گویا کہ طلاق تنجیزی اور طلاق منسوب الی الزمان دونوں متضاد چیزیں ہیں ایک ساتھ جمع نہیں ہوسکتیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے کہا أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ الْيَوْمَ بِأَنْ قَالَ لِامْرَأَتِهِ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ فِى الدَّارِ أَوْ فِى مَكَّةَ وَقَعَ الطَّلَاقُ وَإِنْ لَمْ تَكُنِ الْمَرْأَةُ فِي الدَّارِ وَلَا فِي مَكَّةَ لأَنَّ الطَّلَاقَ لَا يَخْتَصُّ بِمَكَان دُونَ مَكَان فَإِذَا وَقَعَ فِي مَكَانٍ وَقَعَ فِي الْأَمَاكِنِ كُلِّهَا، وَإِنْ دَخَلَتْ عَلَى الزَّمَانِ فَإِنْ كَانَ مَاضِيًا يَقَعُ الطَّلَاقُ فِي الْحَالِ نَحْوُ أَنْ يَقُولَ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ فِي الْأَمْسِ أَوْ فِي الْعَامِ الْمَاضِي لِأَنَّ إِنْشَاء الطَّلَاقِ فِى الزَّمَانِ الْمَاضِي لَا يُتَصَوَّرُ فَيُجْعَلُ إِخْبَارًا أَوْ تَلْغُو الْإِضَافَةُ إِلَى الْمَاضِي وَيَبْقَى قَوْلُهُ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ فَيَقَعُ فِي الْحَالِ وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا كَانَ حَاضِرًا بِأَنْ قَالَ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ فِي هَذَا الْوَقْتِ أَوْ فِي هَذِهِ السَّاعَةِ يَقَعُ فِي الْحَالِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مُسْتَقَبَّلًا لَا يَقَعُ حَتَّى يَأْتِيَ بِأَنْ قَالَ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ فِى غَدٍ أَوْ فِى الشَّهْرِ الْآتِى لِأَنَّ الطَّلَاقَ يَحْتَمِلُ الاخْتِصَاصَ بِوَقْتِ دُونَ وَقْتِ فَإِذَا جُعِلَ الْغَدُ ظَرْفًا لَهُ لَا يَقَعُ قَبْلَهُ. بدائع الصنائع: كتاب الأيمان، فصل فى شرائط رکن الیمین، ج ۳ ص ۲۵، ط: دار الكتب العلمية الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب إيقاع الطلاق، ج ۲ ص ۳۸۲، ط: رحمانیه

غَدًا يَا غَدًا الْيَوْمَ “ تو اس صورت میں پہلے کلمے کا اعتبار ہوگا یعنی شوہر کے منہ سے جو کلام پہلے نکلا ہے اسی پر عمل کیا جائے گا، یعنی پہلی صورت میں چونکہ اس کے منہ سے الیوم پہلے نکلا ہے اس لئے طلاق بھی یوم میں واقع ہوگی ، اور دوسری صورت میں چونکہ غدا‘ پہلے نکلا ہے اس لئے طلاق آئندہ کل واقع ہوگی ۔ پہلی صورت میں جب اس نے الیوم“ پہلے کہا تو گویا کہ یہ طلاق تنجیزی ہے اور طلاق تجیزی اضافت کا احتمال نہیں رکھتی ، لہذا مذکورہ صورت میں بھی یہ طلاق غدا “ کی طرف منسوب ہونے کا احتمال نہ رکھے گی ، اور دوسری صورت میں جب غدا “ کا اعتبار کیا گیا تو طلاق منسوب الى الغد ہوگی اور منسوب شدہ چیز فی الحال واقع نہیں ہو سکتی۔ پہلی صورت میں شوہر نے الیسوم“ کو مقدم رکھا تو طلاق فی الحال واقع ہوگی اور دوسر الفظ لغو ہو گا، اس لئے کہ منجر فوری طور پر واقع ہونے والی شے اضافت اور نسبت کا احتمال نہیں رکھتی ۔ دوسری صورت میں طلاق غد“ کی طرف منسوب ہے اور منسوب شدہ چیز فی الحال واقع نہیں ہو سکتی ، کیونکہ اس میں ایک واقع چیز یعنی اضافت کو خواہ مخواہ باطل کرنا لازم آئے گا جو درست نہیں ، اس لئے طلاق غد“ کی طرف منسوب ہو کر آئندہ کل میں واقع ہوگی ۔
Section on Adding Divorce to Time. (56) Indeed the immediate cannot bear addition, and likewise what is added cannot be immediate. Translation: The divorce that occurs immediately does not have the possibility of addition, and what is added cannot occur immediately. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that immediate divorce, i.e., absolute divorce, cannot be attributed to a time, and similarly a divorce that is attributed to a time cannot be immediate. In other words, immediate divorce and divorce attributed to time are contradictory things; they cannot be combined. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if someone says 'you are divorced today' — by saying to his wife 'you are divorced in the house' or 'in Mecca,' the divorce occurs even if the wife is not in the house or in Mecca, because divorce is not restricted to one place over another. So if it occurs in one place, it occurs in all places. And if it enters upon time, then if it is past, the divorce occurs immediately, such as saying 'you are divorced yesterday' or 'in the past year,' because initiating divorce in the past time is inconceivable, so it is made an announcement or the addition to the past becomes void, and his statement 'you are divorced' remains, so it occurs immediately. Likewise, if it is present, by saying 'you are divorced at this time' or 'in this hour,' it occurs immediately. And if it is future, it does not occur until that time comes, by saying 'you are divorced tomorrow' or 'in the coming month,' because divorce bears the possibility of being restricted to a time rather than a time; so if tomorrow is made a container for it, it does not occur before it. (Badā'i' al-Ṣanā'i') ... 'Tomorrow, O tomorrow, today' — so in this case the first word is considered, i.e., the word that first came out of the husband's mouth is acted upon. So in the first case, since 'today' came out first, the divorce also occurs in the day, and in the second case, since 'tomorrow' came out first, the divorce occurs the next day. In the first case, when he said 'today' first, it is as if this is an immediate divorce, and immediate divorce does not bear addition, so in this case this divorce will not bear being attributed to 'tomorrow.' And in the second case, when 'tomorrow' is considered, the divorce becomes attributed to tomorrow, and what is attributed cannot occur immediately. In the first case, the husband gave precedence to 'today,' so the divorce occurs immediately and the second word becomes void, because the immediate object that occurs instantly does not bear addition and attribution. In the second case, the divorce is attributed to 'tomorrow,' and what is attributed cannot occur immediately, because invalidating the actual thing (i.e., the addition) would necessarily follow, which is not correct, so the divorce is attributed to 'tomorrow' and will occur the next day.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage from Uṣūl al-Hidāyah introduces a key principle in Hanafi divorce law: an immediate divorce (al-munajjiz) cannot be made conditional upon a future time, and a deferred divorce (al-muḍāf) cannot be immediate. The author explains that divorce is not restricted to specific locations, so if a man says 'you are divorced in the house' or 'in Mecca,' the divorce occurs even if she is not there, because divorce is not location-specific. Similarly, with time: mentioning the past or present yields immediate divorce; mentioning the future (like 'tomorrow') delays it. The principle then applies to a case where a man says two contradictory times: if he says 'today, tomorrow,' the first word takes effect (immediate); if 'tomorrow, today,' the second is void and divorce occurs tomorrow. This is because the immediate divorce cannot be added to a future time, so the later time phrase is void. The rulings are drawn from Badā'i' al-Ṣanā'i' and al-Hidāyah.

Key Terms
الْمُنَجِّز (al-munajjiz): The divorce that takes effect immediately upon utterance, without any time condition.
الْمُضَاف (al-muḍāf): The divorce that is attached to a specific future time, e.g., 'you are divorced tomorrow.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife, 'You are divorced today, tomorrow,' when does the divorce occur according to the Hanafi school?
A) Today
B) Tomorrow
C) Both today and tomorrow
D) It does not occur until a court decides

Key Takeaway
An immediate divorce (tanzīz) cannot be added to a future time; a deferred divorce (iḍāfah) cannot be immediate. When conflicting times are mentioned, the first word governs.

Talaq — Divorce

Time Container Does Not Imply Continuity (Ẓarfiyya)
States a principle and applies it to divorce timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a time container does not require occupying the entire duration, and apply it to divorce phrasing scenarios.

Core Idea
When divorce is assigned to a time, it occurs at an instant, not the whole period.

This lesson introduces a key Hanafi principle from Uṣūl al-Hidāyah: the container (ẓarf) of time does not demand covering the entire container. This matters in divorce (ṭalāq) when the husband specifies a time like 'today' or 'tomorrow'. The divorce takes effect at some moment within that time, not necessarily throughout. We will explore the principle and its application through practical examples.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Read the Arabic maxim: إِنَّ الظَّرْفِيَّةَ لَا تَقْتَضِي الْإِسْتِيْعَابَ. Understand its literal meaning: being a container does not require occupying the entire container.
2
Understand the legal effect
The principle means that when a legal act (like divorce) is tied to a time, it does not have to last the whole time. It occurs at any moment within that time window.
This applies to any act attached to a time, not just divorce.
3
Apply to the given examples
Work through the two phrases: 'You are divorced today tomorrow' and 'You are divorced tomorrow today'. Determine which time governs based on the principle of tanzīz (immediacy) versus iḍāfa (addition).
The first time mentioned takes effect; the second is either void or ineffective.

(۵۷) إِنَّ الظَّرْفِيَّةَ لَا تَقْتَضِي الْإِسْتِيْعَابَ. ترجمہ: ظرف ہونا استیعاب کا تقاضا نہیں کرتا۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب کوئی شے ظرف واقع ہو تو یہ ظرف اس کے استیعاب کا تقاضا نہیں کرتا۔
وَإِنْ قَالَ : أَنْتِ طَالِقَ الْيَوْمَ غَدًا فَهِيَ طَالِقٌ الْيَوْمَ ، لأنَّهُ ذَكَرَ وَقَتَيْنِ غَيْرَ مَعْطُوفٍ أَحَدُهُمَا عَلَى الْآخَرِ، وَفِي مِثْلِهِ الْوُقُوعُ فِى أَوَّل الْوَقْتَيْن ذِكْرًا، وَهُوَ الْيَوْمُ، وَلَوْ قَالَ: غَدًا الْيَوْمَ، طَلْقَتْ غَدًا، وَهَذَا، لأنَّ قَوْلَهُ: أَنْتِ طَالِقَ الْيَوْمَ تَنْجِيرٌ وَقَوْلَهُ: غَدًا إِضَافَةٌ إِلَى وَقْتٍ مُنتَظَرٍ، وَالْمُنَجَّزُ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْإِضَافَةَ، فَكَانَ قَوْلُهُ غَدًا لَغْوًا، وَإِذَا قَالَ : أَوَّلًا غَدًا، كَانَ هَذَا إِضَافَةَ الطَّلَاقِ إِلَى وَقْتِ مُنتَظَرٍ، فَلَوْ نَجَّزَ بِذِكْرِهِ الْيَوْمَ لَمْ يَبْقَ مُضَافًا.
المبسوط للسرخسي کتاب الطلاق، ج ۶ ص ۱۱۵، ط: دار المعرفة
الهداية كتاب الطلاق، فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان، ج۲ ص ۳۸۲، ط: رحمانیه
(57) Indeed, being a time container does not require occupying the entire time. Translation: Being a container does not require occupying (the entire duration). Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that when something occurs as a container, this container does not require that it occupy the entire duration. And if he says: 'You are divorced today tomorrow,' then she is divorced today, because he mentioned two times without linking one to the other, and in such a case, the occurrence is at the first of the two times mentioned, which is 'today.' And if he said: 'tomorrow today,' she is divorced tomorrow. This is because his saying 'you are divorced today' is immediate (tanzīz), and his saying 'tomorrow' is an addition to a future time, and the immediate does not bear addition, so his saying 'tomorrow' is void. And when he says first 'tomorrow,' this is adding the divorce to a future time, so if it were made immediate by mentioning 'today,' it would not remain added. (al-Mabsūṭ li'l-Sarakhsī, Kitāb al-Ṭalāq, vol. 6, p. 115) (al-Hidāyah, Kitāb al-Ṭalāq, section on adding divorce to time, vol. 2, p. 382)
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This second principle from Uṣūl al-Hidāyah states that when a divorce is assigned to a time container (ẓarf), it does not require the divorce to occupy the entire duration of that time. For example, if a man says 'you are divorced today,' the divorce occurs at some moment within the day, not necessarily from dawn to dusk. The passage then quotes from al-Mabsūṭ and al-Hidāyah about the case of saying 'today tomorrow' again, but here the focus is on the ẓarfiyya principle. In the quoted passage, the ruling is that if the husband says 'you are divorced today tomorrow,' the divorce occurs today because the immediate divorce cannot be added. But if he says 'tomorrow today,' it occurs tomorrow. This reinforces that the time phrase does not necessitate continuity; the first mentioned time governs, and the divorce occurs at that time without requiring the entire period.

Key Terms
الظَّرْفِيَّةَ (al-ẓarfiyya): The state of being a container (time or place) for an event; here, the time to which divorce is assigned.
الْإِسْتِيْعَاب (al-istī'āb): Occupying or covering the entire duration of the time container.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the Hanafi principle 'al-ẓarfiyyatu lā taqtaḍī al-istī'āb' mean?
A) A time phrase requires the event to last the entire time
B) A time phrase does not require occupying the entire period
C) Divorce is invalid if assigned to a time
D) The time phrase must be pronounced clearly

Key Takeaway
When a legal act is assigned to a time, the Hanafi school holds that it takes effect at some moment within that time, not throughout the entire duration.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Ruling on Divorce Attached to Tomorrow with Specific Intention
Explanation of rulings on divorce attached to future time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a husband says 'Anti taliq fi ghadin' with intention for a specific part, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding judicial acceptance.

Core Idea
The adverb 'fi' does not require the divorce to cover the entire day; the husband's intention determines the exact moment.

When a husband says 'You are divorced tomorrow', the default is that divorce occurs at dawn. But what if he intends the last part of the day? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer based on the linguistic nature of adverbs and the role of intention. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the famous difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance and its attached time
The husband says 'Anti taliq fi ghadin' – 'You are divorced tomorrow'. The key is the phrase 'fi ghadin' (tomorrow).
2
Analyze the linguistic function of 'fi ghadin'
In Hanafi usul, 'fi ghadin' is a zarf (adverb of time). The zarf does not require isti'ab (comprehensiveness) of the mazruf (object). Hence, the divorce does not have to cover the entire day.
This is a key Hanafi principle.
3
Consider the role of intention
If the husband intends a specific part of tomorrow, his intention determines when the divorce takes effect. Abu Hanifa accepts this intention both religiously and judicially.
Intra-Hanafi dispute: Sahibayn accept only religiously.
4
Examine the analogy with fasting
The proof is by analogy: saying 'I fasted in Sha'ban' does not mean fasting the whole month. Similarly, 'fi ghadin' does not imply all parts of tomorrow.
Dalil: Al-Hidayah provides this analogy.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the husband intends the last part, under Abu Hanifa the divorce occurs at that time in court. Under Sahibayn, court presumes dawn but the husband is not sinful.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے یہ کہا أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ فِي غَدٍ “ کہ تجھے آئندہ کل میں طلاق ہے اور اپنے اس کلام سے آئندہ کل کے دن کے آخری حصے کی نیت کی تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس آدمی کی قضاء تصدیق کی جائے گی ، یعنی طلاق آئندہ کل کے آخری حصے میں واقع ہوگی، کیونکہ اس کے کلام میں فِی غَدٍ “یہ ظرف ہے اور طلاق منظروف ہے اور ظرف استیعاب کا تقاضا نہیں کرتا، کلمہ فی ظرفیت کے لئے آتا ہے اور ظرفیت مظروف کے استیعاب کا تقاضا نہیں کرتی ، لہذا فی الغد “ کے جس جزء میں بھی شوہر طلاق کی نیت کرے گاوہ نیت معتبر ہوگی اور اُسی وقت طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ (۵۸) إِنَّ الْإِنْشَاء فِى الْمَاضِي إِنْشَاءُ فِي الْحَالِ . ترجمہ: زمانہ ماضی میں انشاء فی الکلام یہ حال میں انشاء فی الکلام ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ماضی کے انشاء کو حال میں بھی انشاء تسلیم کر لیا جاتا ہے یعنی ماضی میں ثابت ہونے والے کسی حکم کو حال میں بھی ثابت اور نافذ مانتے ہیں جب کسی شے کی نسبت ایسی منافی حالت کی طرف کی جائے جسے خبر بنانا ممکن نہ ہوتو پھر وہ انشاء ہوتا ہے اور انشاء فی الماضی انشاء فی الحال ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا انتِ طَالِقٌ أَمس “ کہ تجھے گزشتہ کل طلاق ہے ، جبکہ اس شخص نے اس عورت سے گزشتہ کل کے ابتدائی حصے میں شادی کی تھی تو اسی وقت طلاق پڑے گی، کیونکہ شوہر کا یہ کلام انشاء فی الماضی ہے اور ہر وَإِنْ قَالَ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ فِي غَدٍ وَقَعَ عَلَيْهَا الطَّلَاقُ بِطُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ فَإِنْ قَالَ نَوَيْتُ بِهِ آخِرَ النَّهَارِ صُدِّقَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ دِيَانَةً وَقَضَاء وَعِنْدَهُمَا لَا يُصَدَّقُ فِى الْقَضَاءِ وَبَدِينُ فِيمَا بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ اللَّهِ لَّا بِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ جَعَلَ الْعَدَ ظَرْفًا لِوُقُوعِ الطَّلَاقِ فِيهِ وَكَوْنُهُ ظَرُفًا لَا يَقْتَضِي كَوْنَهَا مُطَلَّقَةً فِي جَمِيعِ أَجْزَائِهِ، لِأَنَّ الطَّرْفِيَّةَ لَا تَقْتَضِى الاسْتِيعَابَ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّكَ إِذَا قُلْت صُمت فِي شَعْبَانَ لَا يَقْتَضِى أَنْ تَكُونَ صَائِمًا فِي جَمِيعِهِ. الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب الطلاق، ج ۲ ص ۴۴، ط: المطبعة الخيرية الهداية كتاب الطلاق، فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان ج ۲ ص ۳۸۲، ط: رحمانیه اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی انشاء فی الماضی انشاء فی الحال ہوتا ہے، لہذا اس کا یہ کلام بھی انشاء فی الحال ہو گا یعنی گویا کہ یہ ابھی اسی وقت میں اس کو طلاق دے رہا ہے۔ لہذا أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ أَمْس “ سے ماضی والا انشاء أَنْتِ طَالِق الآن‘ یا فی الحال “ کے معنی میں ہو گا اور اسی وقت طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔
Usool-e-Hidayah, volume two: The author of Hidayah mentioned the following principle: If someone said to his wife 'Anti taliq fi ghadin' (You are divorced tomorrow) and intended by this the last part of tomorrow, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa he will be believed in court, meaning divorce occurs in the last part of tomorrow. Because in his speech, 'fi ghadin' is an adverb and divorce is the object. The adverb does not require comprehensiveness. The word 'fi' denotes containment, and containment does not require the object to fill the entire container. Therefore, in whichever part of 'fi al-ghad' the husband intends divorce, his intention is valid and divorce occurs at that time. (58) 'Inna al-insha'a fi al-madi insha'un fi al-hal.' Translation: Insha' in the past tense is insha' in the present. Explanation: The meaning is that insha' in the past is also accepted as insha' in the present. That is, a ruling established in the past is considered established and effective in the present when a thing is attributed to a contradictory state that cannot be made into a report. Then it is insha', and insha' fi al-madi is insha' fi al-hal. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains: If someone said to his wife 'Anti taliq ams' (You are divorced yesterday) while he had married her at the beginning of yesterday, then divorce occurs immediately. Because the husband's utterance is insha' fi al-madi. And whoever said 'Anti taliq fi ghadin', divorce occurs at dawn. If he said 'I intended thereby the end of the day', he is believed according to Abu Hanifa both religiously and judicially, but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he is not believed judicially, only religiously. Because Abu Hanifa made 'al-ghad' an adverb for the occurrence of divorce, and being an adverb does not require that she be divorced in all its parts, because adverbiality does not require comprehensiveness. Do you not see that if you say 'I fasted in Sha'ban', it does not require that you be fasting in all of it. (Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, book of divorce, vol. 2 p. 44; Al-Hidaya, book of divorce, chapter on attaching divorce to time, vol. 2 p. 382) Usool-e-Hidayah, volume two: Insha' fi al-madi is insha' fi al-hal, so his utterance is also insha' fi al-hal, meaning as if he is divorcing her now. Therefore, 'Anti taliq ams' from the past insha' means 'Anti taliq al-an' or 'fi al-hal', and divorce occurs immediately.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage from Usool-e-Hidayah presents two related rulings. First, it explains the ruling when a husband says 'You are divorced tomorrow' and intends a specific part of tomorrow. Abu Hanifa holds that his intention is accepted in court because the word 'fi' (in) indicates containment, not that the divorce covers the entire day. The adverb 'tomorrow' does not require the divorce to occur throughout the entire day; rather, it is sufficient that the divorce occurs at any part of it. This is supported by analogy: saying 'I fasted in Sha'ban' does not mean fasting the whole month. Second, the passage introduces the principle (58): 'Insha' in the past tense is insha' in the present.' This means that when someone uses a past tense verb to create a legal effect (like divorce) that cannot be a true report (because it contradicts known facts), it is treated as a performative utterance taking effect immediately. The application is: if a husband says 'You are divorced yesterday' while the marriage existed yesterday, the divorce occurs immediately because the statement cannot be a report (since the marriage was intact then), so it becomes an insha' taking effect now. The passage also includes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa accepts the husband's intention regarding 'tomorrow' in court, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad only accept it religiously.

Key Terms
ظرف (zarf): An adverb of time or place; here specifically 'fi ghadin' as an adverb of time.
استیعاب (isti'ab): Comprehensiveness; the requirement that the object fill the entire container/time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a husband says 'Anti taliq fi ghadin' and intends the last part of tomorrow, what is the ruling regarding his intention in court?
A) It is not accepted; divorce occurs at dawn.
B) It is accepted, and divorce occurs at the intended time.
C) It is accepted only religiously, not judicially.
D) The husband must repeat the divorce at the intended time.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that an adverb of time does not require comprehensiveness allows the husband's intention to specify the exact moment of divorce, with Abu Hanifa's view being the operative one in fatwa.

The Principle of Insha' in Past Tense as Insha' in Present
Explanation of the principle of insha' in past tense as insha' in present, applied to divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the principle 'Inna al-insha'a fi al-madi insha'un fi al-hal' and apply it to the case of divorce attached to past time.

Core Idea
A past tense utterance that cannot be a true report becomes a performative act taking effect immediately.

When a husband says 'You are divorced yesterday', the statement seems contradictory because the marriage existed yesterday. The Hanafi principle resolves this by treating such utterances as performative acts in the present. This lesson unpacks the rule and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance
The husband says 'Anti taliq ams' – 'You are divorced yesterday'. The key is the past time reference.
2
Determine if it can be a true report
Since the marriage existed yesterday, a divorce at that time would be impossible. Thus, the utterance cannot be khabar (report).
If it could be a report, the principle does not apply.
3
Apply the principle of insha' fi al-madi
Hanafi usul states: 'Inna al-insha'a fi al-madi insha'un fi al-hal' – an insha' in the past tense is treated as insha' in the present.
This rule covers all legal acts, not just divorce.
4
Derive the ruling
Therefore, the utterance is treated as divorce taking effect immediately, at the moment of utterance.
Divorce occurs now.
5
Note the practical implication
The divorce is valid and effective immediately, even though the husband used past tense.
The 'iddah begins from the moment of utterance.

حصے کی نیت کی تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس آدمی کی قضاء تصدیق کی جائے گی ، یعنی طلاق آئندہ کل کے آخری حصے میں واقع ہوگی، کیونکہ اس کے کلام میں فِی غَدٍ “یہ ظرف ہے اور طلاق منظروف ہے اور ظرف استیعاب کا تقاضا نہیں کرتا، کلمہ فی ظرفیت کے لئے آتا ہے اور ظرفیت مظروف کے استیعاب کا تقاضا نہیں کرتی ، لہذا فی الغد “ کے جس جزء میں بھی شوہر طلاق کی نیت کرے گاوہ نیت معتبر ہوگی اور اُسی وقت طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ (۵۸) إِنَّ الْإِنْشَاء فِى الْمَاضِي إِنْشَاءُ فِي الْحَالِ . ترجمہ: زمانہ ماضی میں انشاء فی الکلام یہ حال میں انشاء فی الکلام ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ماضی کے انشاء کو حال میں بھی انشاء تسلیم کر لیا جاتا ہے یعنی ماضی میں ثابت ہونے والے کسی حکم کو حال میں بھی ثابت اور نافذ مانتے ہیں جب کسی شے کی نسبت ایسی منافی حالت کی طرف کی جائے جسے خبر بنانا ممکن نہ ہوتو پھر وہ انشاء ہوتا ہے اور انشاء فی الماضی انشاء فی الحال ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا انتِ طَالِقٌ أَمس “ کہ تجھے گزشتہ کل طلاق ہے ، جبکہ اس شخص نے اس عورت سے گزشتہ کل کے ابتدائی حصے میں شادی کی تھی تو اسی وقت طلاق پڑے گی، کیونکہ شوہر کا یہ کلام انشاء فی الماضی ہے اور ہر وَإِنْ قَالَ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ فِي غَدٍ وَقَعَ عَلَيْهَا الطَّلَاقُ بِطُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ فَإِنْ قَالَ نَوَيْتُ بِهِ آخِرَ النَّهَارِ صُدِّقَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ دِيَانَةً وَقَضَاء وَعِنْدَهُمَا لَا يُصَدَّقُ فِى الْقَضَاءِ وَبَدِينُ فِيمَا بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ اللَّهِ لَّا بِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ جَعَلَ الْعَدَ ظَرْفًا لِوُقُوعِ الطَّلَاقِ فِيهِ وَكَوْنُهُ ظَرُفًا لَا يَقْتَضِي كَوْنَهَا مُطَلَّقَةً فِي جَمِيعِ أَجْزَائِهِ، لِأَنَّ الطَّرْفِيَّةَ لَا تَقْتَضِى الاسْتِيعَابَ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّكَ إِذَا قُلْت صُمت فِي شَعْبَانَ لَا يَقْتَضِى أَنْ تَكُونَ صَائِمًا فِي جَمِيعِهِ. الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب الطلاق، ج ۲ ص ۴۴، ط: المطبعة الخيرية الهداية كتاب الطلاق، فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان ج ۲ ص ۳۸۲، ط: رحمانیه اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی انشاء فی الماضی انشاء فی الحال ہوتا ہے، لہذا اس کا یہ کلام بھی انشاء فی الحال ہو گا یعنی گویا کہ یہ ابھی اسی وقت میں اس کو طلاق دے رہا ہے۔ لہذا أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ أَمْس “ سے ماضی والا انشاء أَنْتِ طَالِق الآن‘ یا فی الحال “ کے معنی میں ہو گا اور اسی وقت طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔
Usool-e-Hidayah, volume two: The author of Hidayah mentioned the following principle: If someone said to his wife 'Anti taliq fi ghadin' (You are divorced tomorrow) and intended by this the last part of tomorrow, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa he will be believed in court, meaning divorce occurs in the last part of tomorrow. Because in his speech, 'fi ghadin' is an adverb and divorce is the object. The adverb does not require comprehensiveness. The word 'fi' denotes containment, and containment does not require the object to fill the entire container. Therefore, in whichever part of 'fi al-ghad' the husband intends divorce, his intention is valid and divorce occurs at that time. (58) 'Inna al-insha'a fi al-madi insha'un fi al-hal.' Translation: Insha' in the past tense is insha' in the present. Explanation: The meaning is that insha' in the past is also accepted as insha' in the present. That is, a ruling established in the past is considered established and effective in the present when a thing is attributed to a contradictory state that cannot be made into a report. Then it is insha', and insha' fi al-madi is insha' fi al-hal. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains: If someone said to his wife 'Anti taliq ams' (You are divorced yesterday) while he had married her at the beginning of yesterday, then divorce occurs immediately. Because the husband's utterance is insha' fi al-madi. And whoever said 'Anti taliq fi ghadin', divorce occurs at dawn. If he said 'I intended thereby the end of the day', he is believed according to Abu Hanifa both religiously and judicially, but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he is not believed judicially, only religiously. Because Abu Hanifa made 'al-ghad' an adverb for the occurrence of divorce, and being an adverb does not require that she be divorced in all its parts, because adverbiality does not require comprehensiveness. Do you not see that if you say 'I fasted in Sha'ban', it does not require that you be fasting in all of it. (Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, book of divorce, vol. 2 p. 44; Al-Hidaya, book of divorce, chapter on attaching divorce to time, vol. 2 p. 382) Usool-e-Hidayah, volume two: Insha' fi al-madi is insha' fi al-hal, so his utterance is also insha' fi al-hal, meaning as if he is divorcing her now. Therefore, 'Anti taliq ams' from the past insha' means 'Anti taliq al-an' or 'fi al-hal', and divorce occurs immediately.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage from Usool-e-Hidayah presents two related rulings. First, it explains the ruling when a husband says 'You are divorced tomorrow' and intends a specific part of tomorrow. Abu Hanifa holds that his intention is accepted in court because the word 'fi' (in) indicates containment, not that the divorce covers the entire day. The adverb 'tomorrow' does not require the divorce to occur throughout the entire day; rather, it is sufficient that the divorce occurs at any part of it. This is supported by analogy: saying 'I fasted in Sha'ban' does not mean fasting the whole month. Second, the passage introduces the principle (58): 'Insha' in the past tense is insha' in the present.' This means that when someone uses a past tense verb to create a legal effect (like divorce) that cannot be a true report (because it contradicts known facts), it is treated as a performative utterance taking effect immediately. The application is: if a husband says 'You are divorced yesterday' while the marriage existed yesterday, the divorce occurs immediately because the statement cannot be a report (since the marriage was intact then), so it becomes an insha' taking effect now. The passage also includes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa accepts the husband's intention regarding 'tomorrow' in court, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad only accept it religiously.

Key Terms
انشاء (insha'): A performative utterance that creates a legal effect, as opposed to khabar (report).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a divorce take effect if a husband says 'Anti taliq ams' (you are divorced yesterday) and the marriage existed yesterday?
A) Yesterday.
B) Immediately upon utterance.
C) Not at all.
D) Only if he intends it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle 'insha' fi al-madi insha' fi al-hal' converts past tense performative utterances into present effect, ensuring legal acts are not invalidated by tense alone.

The Meaning of 'Yawm' Depending on Verb Type
Definition of 'yawm' and application to talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle for interpreting 'yawm' when attached to extended vs. non-extended actions, and apply it to a conditional divorce case.

Core Idea
Yawm means daytime with extended actions, but absolute time with instantaneous actions.

The Arabic word 'yawm' (day) can have different meanings depending on the verb it accompanies. The Hanafi school, through its attention to linguistic context, derived a precise rule: if 'yawm' is paired with an action that takes time (mumtadd), it refers to daylight hours; if paired with an instantaneous action (ghayr mumtadd), it means any time or moment. This distinction matters greatly in conditional statements, especially in matters of divorce (talaq). The following passage from Al-Hidayah explains this principle and its application to a man who marries at night after uttering a conditional divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic categories
Understand the two types of actions: extended (fi'l mumtadd — takes time, e.g., fasting) and non-extended (fi'l ghayr mumtadd — instantaneous, e.g., marriage, divorce).
These categories determine the interpretation of 'yawm'.
2
Memorize the core principle
State the Hanafi rule: When 'yawm' is coupled with an extended action, it means daytime; when with a non-extended action, it means absolute time (any 24-hour period).
This is a definitive rule in the school.
3
Apply to the divorce scenario
Consider the statement: 'Yawm atazawwajuki fa-anti taliq' (The day I marry you, you are divorced). Since marriage (nikah) is non-extended, 'yawm' means absolute time, so the divorce occurs even if the marriage takes place at night.
The outcome is immediate divorce at the moment of marriage.
4
Differentiate with an extended action example
Contrast with: 'Yawm asumu fa-anti taliq' (The day I fast, you are divorced). Fasting is extended, so 'yawm' means daytime. If he fasts only from dawn to dusk, divorce occurs at the start of fasting? Actually, the fasting begins at dawn, so if he starts fasting at night, it may not count? But the principle: if he fasts during the day, divorce occurs; if he fasts at night (invalid), divorce does not occur because it's not daytime.
This shows the practical difference.
5
Confirm the ruling
According to Al-Hidayah, the mufta bihi position is that divorce occurs at the time of marriage, whether day or night, because 'yawm' is interpreted as absolute time due to the non-extended action.
This is the school's relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۹) إِنَّ الْيَوْمَ إِذَا قُرِنَ بِفِعْلٍ يَمْتَدُّ يُرَادُ بِهِ بِيَاضُ النَّهَارِ وَإِذَا قُرِنَ بِفِعْلٍ لَا يَمْتَدُّ يُرَادُ بِهِ مُطْلَقُ الْوَقْتِ . ترجمہ: یوم جب فعل ممتد کے ساتھ مل جائے تو اس سے دن کی سفیدی مراد ہوتی ہے اور جب فعل غیر ممتد کے ساتھ مل جائے تو اس سے مطلق وقت مراد ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ لفظ یوم جب ایسے فعل کے ساتھ مقترن ہو جائے کہ وہ فعل ممتد ہو یعنی اس کو سرانجام دینے میں وقت لگتا ہو تو اس وقت یوم سے مراد دن ہوگا اور اگر یوم غیر ممتد فعل کے ساتھ مقترن ہو جائے تو اس وقت یوم سے مطلق وقت مراد ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے عورت سے یہ کہا یوم أَتَزَوَّجُكِ فَأَنْتِ طَالِقٌ “ کہ جس دن میں آپ سے شادی کروں گا تجھے طلاق ہے۔ پھر اس شخص نے اس کے ساتھ رات میں شادی کی تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی کیونکہ اس شخص کے کلام میں یوم فعل غیر ممتد کے ساتھ مقترن ہے اور جب یوم فعل غیر ممتد کے ساتھ مقترن ہو تو یوم سے مطلق وقت مراد ہوتا ہے، لہذا اس آدمی کے کلام میں بھی یوم سے مراد مطلق وقت ہو گا، جب یوم سے مطلق وقت مراد ہے تو یہ دن کو بھی شامل ہے اور رات کو بھی ۔ یادر ہے کہ فعل غیرمند سے مراد ایسا فعل اور کام ہے جس کی انجام دہی میں زیادہ وقت نہ لگتا ہو، جیسے دخول، خروج وغیرہ۔ طلاق بھی اسی قبیل سے ہے اور اسے بھی واقع کرنے میں زیادہ وقت نہیں لگتا، اس لئے یوم کے اس (قَوْلُهُ: وَإِنْ نَكَحَهَا قَبْلَ أَمْسِ وَقَعَ الْآنَ لأَنَّهُ أَسْنَدَهُ إِلَى حَالَةٍ مُنَافِيَةٍ وَلَا يُمْكِنُ تَصْحِيحُهُ إِخْبَارًا أَيْضًا فَكَانَ إِنْشَاء وَالْإِنْشَاء فِي الْمَاضِي إِنْشَاءُ فِي الْحَالِ فَيَقَعُ السَّاعَةَ. البحر الرائق كتاب الطلاق، فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلي الزمان، ج۳، ص ۲۹۳ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي الهداية كتاب الطلاق، فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان، ج۲ ص ۳۸۴، ط: رحمانیه
(59) 'Inna al-yawma idha qurina bi-fi'lin yamtaddu yuraddu bihi bayadu al-nahari wa idha qurina bi-fi'lin la yamtaddu yuraddu bihi mutlaqu al-waqti.' Translation: When 'yawm' is coupled with an extended action, it means the whiteness of the day; when coupled with a non-extended action, it means absolute time. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that the word 'yawm' when accompanied by an action that takes time, then 'yawm' means the day; but if accompanied by an action that does not take time, then 'yawm' means absolute time. The author of Hidayah, mentioning this principle, explains: If someone said to a woman 'Yawm atazawwajuki fa-anti taliq' (The day I marry you, you are divorced), then he married her at night, divorce occurs. Because in his speech, 'yawm' is accompanied by a non-extended action, and when 'yawm' is accompanied by a non-extended action, it means absolute time. Therefore, in this man's statement, 'yawm' means absolute time, which includes both day and night. Note that non-extended action refers to an action that does not take much time to perform, such as entering, exiting, etc. Divorce is also of this type; it does not take much time to occur. Hence, regarding this 'yawm', (then quote from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and Al-Hidayah).
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage introduces a linguistic-legal principle (59) regarding the word 'yawm' (day). The principle states that when 'yawm' is attached to an action that takes time (mumtadd), it refers specifically to the daytime (bayad al-nahar). But when attached to an action that does not take time (ghayr mumtadd), it refers to any time (mutlaq al-waqt). The author applies this to a conditional divorce: if a man says 'The day I marry you, you are divorced,' and he marries at night, divorce occurs immediately because 'yawm' here is attached to the act of marriage (nikah), which is a non-extended action (it does not take much time). Thus, 'yawm' includes both day and night. The passage also clarifies that divorce itself is a non-extended action, consistent with this principle.

Key Terms
یوم (yawm): The word 'day', which can mean either the daytime or any 24-hour period depending on the verb it accompanies.
فعل ممتد (fi'l mumtadd): An action that takes time to perform, e.g., fasting.
فعل غیر ممتد (fi'l ghayr mumtadd): An instantaneous action that does not take time, e.g., marriage, divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to a woman 'Yawm atazawwajuki fa-anti taliq' and marries her at night, when does divorce occur according to this principle?
A) At dawn of the next day.
B) At the moment of marriage, because 'yawm' means absolute time.
C) It does not occur because night is not considered a day.
D) Only if he intended night.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school interprets 'yawm' contextually: daytime with extended actions, absolute time with instantaneous actions, critically affecting the timing of conditional divorces.

The Meaning of Yawm with Extended vs Non-Extended Actions
Explaining the Hidayah principle on interpreting 'yawm' in divorce conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that distinguishes the meaning of 'yawm' in conditional divorces based on whether the conjoined action is extended or non-extended.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, 'yawm' means daytime when linked to an extended act, but any moment when linked to an instantaneous act.

Conditional divorces often hinge on the word 'yawm' (day). Is it the entire day, just the daylight, or any instant? The Hanafi school provides a precise rule: the meaning shifts depending on the nature of the accompanying action. This lesson unpacks that rule from al-Hidayah, giving you a clear tool for real-life divorce scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
State the Hidayah principle: 'yawm' with an extended action (like fasting) means daytime; with a non-extended action (like marriage) means absolute time.
2
Define 'extended' and 'non-extended'
Extended actions take time (e.g., fasting, pilgrimage). Non-extended actions are instantaneous (e.g., divorce, marriage, entering a house). Classify the action in the condition.
Note: 'non-extended' does not mean literally zero time, but that the action is not inherently time-consuming.
3
Apply to a concrete example
Take the case: 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced.' Marriage is non-extended, so 'yawm' means absolute time. Therefore, marrying at night triggers divorce.
This contrasts with a literal interpretation that would require daytime.
4
Understand the rationale (talil)
An extended action needs a measurable duration (daytime) to be meaningful; a non-extended action only needs any moment. The Hanafi principle respects this logical fit.
This is a form of talil (legal reasoning based on suitability).
5
Recognize the Hanafi uniqueness
Other schools might take 'yawm' literally as daytime in all contexts. The Hanafi differentiation is a hallmark of their focus on the accompanying action's nature.
This principle is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی انشاء فی الماضی انشاء فی الحال ہوتا ہے، لہذا اس کا یہ کلام بھی انشاء فی الحال ہو گا یعنی گویا کہ یہ ابھی اسی وقت میں اس کو طلاق دے رہا ہے۔ لہذا أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ أَمْس “ سے ماضی والا انشاء أَنْتِ طَالِق الآن‘ یا فی الحال “ کے معنی میں ہو گا اور اسی وقت طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ (۵۹) إِنَّ الْيَوْمَ إِذَا قُرِنَ بِفِعْلٍ يَمْتَدُّ يُرَادُ بِهِ بِيَاضُ النَّهَارِ وَإِذَا قُرِنَ بِفِعْلٍ لَا يَمْتَدُّ يُرَادُ بِهِ مُطْلَقُ الْوَقْتِ .
ترجمہ: یوم جب فعل ممتد کے ساتھ مل جائے تو اس سے دن کی سفیدی مراد ہوتی ہے اور جب فعل غیر ممتد کے ساتھ مل جائے تو اس سے مطلق وقت مراد ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ لفظ یوم جب ایسے فعل کے ساتھ مقترن ہو جائے کہ وہ فعل ممتد ہو یعنی اس کو سرانجام دینے میں وقت لگتا ہو تو اس وقت یوم سے مراد دن ہوگا اور اگر یوم غیر ممتد فعل کے ساتھ مقترن ہو جائے تو اس وقت یوم سے مطلق وقت مراد ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے عورت سے یہ کہا یوم أَتَزَوَّجُكِ فَأَنْتِ طَالِقٌ کہ جس دن میں آپ سے شادی کروں گا تجھے طلاق ہے۔ پھر اس شخص نے اس کے ساتھ رات میں شادی کی تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی کیونکہ اس شخص کے کلام میں یوم فعل غیر ممتد کے ساتھ مقترن ہے اور جب یوم فعل غیر ممتد کے ساتھ مقترن ہو تو یوم سے مطلق وقت مراد ہوتا ہے، لہذا اس آدمی کے کلام میں بھی یوم سے مراد مطلق وقت ہو گا، جب یوم سے مطلق وقت مراد ہے تو یہ دن کو بھی شامل ہے اور رات کو بھی ۔ یادر ہے کہ فعل غیرمند سے مراد ایسا فعل اور کام ہے جس کی انجام دہی میں زیادہ وقت نہ لگتا ہو، جیسے دخول، خروج وغیرہ۔ طلاق بھی اسی قبیل سے ہے اور اسے بھی واقع کرنے میں زیادہ وقت نہیں لگتا، اس لئے یوم کے اس (قَوْلُهُ: وَإِنْ نَكَحَهَا قَبْلَ أَمْسِ وَقَعَ الْآنَ لأَنَّهُ أَسْنَدَهُ إِلَى حَالَةٍ مُنَافِيَةٍ وَلَا يُمْكِنُ تَصْحِيحُهُ إِخْبَارًا أَيْضًا فَكَانَ إِنْشَاء وَالْإِنْشَاء فِي الْمَاضِي إِنْشَاءُ فِي الْحَالِ فَيَقَعُ السَّاعَةَ. البحر الرائق كتاب الطلاق، فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلي الزمان، ج۳، ص ۲۹۳ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
الهداية كتاب الطلاق، فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان، ج۲ ص ۳۸۴، ط: رحمانیه

اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی
کے ساتھ مقارن ہونے کی صورت میں مطلق وقت مراد ہوگا اور رات دن میں جس وقت بھی نکاح کرے طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اور اگر لفظ یوم ایسے فعل اور کام کے ساتھ متصل ہو جس کے کرنے میں وقت لگتا ہو جیسے روزہ ، تو اس صورت میں یوم سے مراد بیاض نہار ہوگا، اس لئے کہ اس وقت یوم سے مراد معیار ہوگا۔

The principles of Hidayah, Volume Two. Insha in the past is insha in the present; therefore his speech is also insha in the present, i.e., it is as if he is divorcing her at that very moment. So 'You are divorced yesterday' is insha in the past meaning 'You are divorced now' or 'at present', and divorce occurs immediately. (59) Indeed, 'yawm' when conjoined with an extended action is intended to mean the brightness of the daytime, and when conjoined with a non-extended action is intended to mean absolute time. Translation: When 'yawm' is joined with an extended action, its meaning is the whiteness of day, and when joined with a non-extended action, its meaning is absolute time. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that the word 'yawm' when accompanied by a action that is extended, i.e., takes time to perform, then 'yawm' means daytime; if 'yawm' is accompanied by a non-extended action, then 'yawm' means absolute time. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain: if a man says to his wife 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced', and then he marries her at night, the divorce occurs because in his speech 'yawm' is accompanied by a non-extended action, and when 'yawm' is accompanied by a non-extended action, it means absolute time. Therefore, in this man's speech, 'yawm' means absolute time, and since it means absolute time, it includes both day and night. Note that a non-extended action refers to an action that does not take much time, such as entering, exiting, etc. Divorce is also of this category; it does not take much time to occur, therefore 'yawm' in this context (His statement: 'And if he married her before yesterday, it occurs now because he attributed it to a contradictory state, and it is also not possible to validate it as a report, so it is insha, and insha in the past is insha in the present, so it occurs at that hour.' - al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Book of Divorce, Chapter on Adding Divorce to Time, vol. 3, p. 293, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami; al-Hidayah, Book of Divorce, Chapter on Adding Divorce to Time, vol. 2, p. 384, Rahmaniyyah edition. Usool e Hidayah, Volume Two: 'When it is accompanied, absolute time is meant, and whenever he marries, whether by day or night, divorce occurs. And if the word 'yawm' is connected to an action that takes time, like fasting, then 'yawm' means the brightness of daytime, because at that time 'yawm' is intended as a measure.' And whoever says to a woman: 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced', and marries her at night, she is divorced because 'yawm' is mentioned and intended to mean the brightness of daytime. So it is interpreted (i.e., the brightness of daytime) when (the day) is conjoined with an extended action, like fasting, which is extended. And the command (in the hand, as in his saying 'your affair is in your hand on the day so-and-so arrives') because by it the measure is intended. He intended by 'yawm' the measure when the action is extended, and the intended meaning of measure is that it is an amount corresponding to the action, like fasting in a day. And it is more suitable for him, i.e., that the measure be intended from the day is more appropriate for the extended action, because the extended action needs a specific time, which is the brightness of daytime that became the expression for the measure. This differs from when the action is not extended, as it does not need a prolonged time, but absolute time suffices. - al-Binayah, Book of Divorce, Chapter on Adding Divorce to Time, vol. 5, p. 330, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah; al-Hidayah, Book of Divorce, Chapter on Adding Divorce to Time, vol. 2, p. 384, Rahmaniyyah edition.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on a principle from the Hidayah regarding the interpretation of the word 'yawm' (day) when used in a conditional divorce. The author first explains that when 'yawm' is used with an extended action (an action that takes time, like fasting), it means the actual daytime (the brightness of the day). When used with a non-extended action (an action that is instantaneous, like marriage or divorce), it means absolute time, including both day and night. The author gives the example: if a man says to a woman 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced' and then marries her at night, the divorce takes effect because 'yawm' is taken as absolute time. The commentary also includes a quote from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Hidayah on a related matter about attributing divorce to the past, and then continues on the next page reinforcing that when 'yawm' is linked to a non-extended action, absolute time is meant. Finally, a footnote from al-Binayah explains the same principle in Arabic: if a man says 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced' and marries at night, she is divorced; the word 'yawm' when used with an extended action like fasting means the daytime, but when used with a non-extended action like marriage, it means absolute time. The commentator emphasizes that the Hanafi position is based on the nature of the action: extended actions require a specific measure of time (daytime), while non-extended actions only require any moment.

Key Terms
يَوْم (yawm): In this principle, 'yawm' can mean either the daytime (brightness of the day) or absolute time, depending on the action it accompanies.
فِعْلٌ يَمْتَدُّ (fi'lun yamtaddu): An action that is prolonged and takes time, such as fasting (sawm).
فِعْلٌ لَا يَمْتَدُّ (fi'lun la yamtaddu): An action that is instantaneous and does not take time, such as marriage (nikah) or divorce (talaq).
بِيَاضُ النَّهَارِ (bayadu al-nahar): The brightness of daytime, i.e., the actual daylight hours.
مُطْلَقُ الْوَقْتِ (mutlaqu al-waqt): Absolute time, meaning any moment without specification of day or night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Yes, because 'yawm' with a non-extended action means absolute time.
C) No, because marriage is not a valid condition for divorce.
D) Yes, but only if the marriage is performed during the day.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle: 'yawm' means daytime when conjoined with an extended action, but absolute time when conjoined with a non-extended action.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Talaq is for Removing the Wife's Restraint, Not the Husband's
Defining the purpose of talaq and contrasting it with ibaanah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that talaq removes the wife's marital restraint and apply it to determine whether a husband's self-referencing divorce statement is effective.

Core Idea
Talaq removes the wife's marital restraint; a husband's statement 'I am divorced' does not effect talaq.

The Hanafi school defines talaq (divorce) by its purpose: it removes the restraint (qayd) that marriage places on the wife, freeing her to marry others after her iddah. This is fundamentally different from ibaanah (separation), which removes the wuslah (connection) between spouses entirely. This distinction has a critical practical consequence: if a husband says to his wife 'I am divorced from you' (ana minki taliqun), no divorce occurs—even if he intended it—because the words refer to his own status, not the wife's restraint.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition of talaq
Talaq is defined as the removal of the qayd (restraint) that marriage imposes on the wife. This qayd is the restriction that prevents her from marrying other men. The subject of the action is the wife's restraint.
The term qayd is key: it is something that binds the wife, not the husband.
2
Contrast talaq with ibaanah
Ibaanah removes the wuslah (connection/bond) between husband and wife. While both end the marriage, ibaanah targets the relationship itself, whereas talaq targets the wife's individual restriction.
Khul' is a form of ibaanah.
3
Apply the principle to the case of 'ana minki taliqun'
The husband says 'I am divorced from you.' Since talaq removes the wife's restraint, the words must address that restraint. Here, the husband speaks about himself, so the statement is ineffective—no talaq occurs.
This is a defining example in al-Hidayah.
4
Understand the supporting rationale
The husband is not restricted by marriage in the same way—he may marry up to four wives. Therefore, 'removing his restraint' is meaningless. The focus is solely on the wife's position.
This underscores that talaq is wife-centric.

(20) Indeed, talaq is for removing the restraint, unlike ibaanah, for it is for removing the connection. Translation: Talaq is for removing the restraint (marriage), unlike ibaanah (separation), because ibaanah is for removing the bond and connection. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that talaq is for removing that restriction and bond that is imposed on the woman due to marriage, unlike ibaanah, i.e., separation, whereby the relationship and bond between husband and wife is terminated. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain: if a man says to his wife 'I am divorced from you', then in this case talaq does not occur, even if the husband intended divorce by his words, because talaq is to remove the restraint that is on the woman, not on the husband. Do you not know that for the husband, marriage to two, three, or four women (is permitted). al-Hidayah, Book of Divorce, Chapter on Adding Divorce to Time, vol. 2, p. 384, Rahmaniyyah edition.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents a principle from al-Hidayah clarifying the essential nature of talaq (divorce) versus ibaanah (separation). The principle states that talaq is meant to remove the 'qayd' (restraint or limitation) that marriage places on the wife. In contrast, ibaanah (which here refers to a complete separation like khul' or permanent separation) removes the 'wuslah' (connection or bond) between husband and wife. The practical application given is: if a husband says to his wife 'I am divorced from you' (ana minki taliqun), no divorce occurs even if he intends it. The reason is that divorce operates on the wife's restraint, not the husband's; the husband is not restricted in terms of being able to marry multiple women (up to four), so the statement is meaningless as a divorce. The commentator emphasizes that the subject of divorce is the wife's marital restriction, and therefore the wording must address her directly. This principle reinforces that talaq is wife-specific.

Key Terms
طَلَاق (talaq): Divorce that removes the marital restraint (qayd) from the wife, allowing her to remarry after iddah.
إِبَانَة (ibaanah): Separation that removes the marital connection (wuslah) entirely, such as khul' or permanent separation, ending all ties.
قَيْد (qayd): The restraint or restriction that marriage imposes on the wife, preventing her from marrying others.
وُصْلَة (wuslah): The bond or connection between husband and wife that exists in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Talaq occurs because the husband used a form of the word talaq.
B) Talaq does not occur because the statement refers to the husband's own restraint, not the wife's.
C) Talaq occurs only if the wife accepts the pronouncement.
D) Ibaanah occurs, not talaq.

Key Takeaway
Talaq is specifically designed to remove the wife's marital restraint (qayd); therefore, any divorce wording must target her restraint, not the husband's.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Talaq Removes Restriction on Wife, Ibanah Removes Shared Connection
Explains why 'I am divorced from you' does not effect talaq while 'I am separate' does

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between qayd and wusla to determine whether a given expression of divorce effects talaq.

Core Idea
Talaq removes the wife's restriction; 'I am divorced' fails because it targets the husband.

This lesson from al-Hidayah clarifies a subtle but critical point in the wording of talaq. Not every expression a husband uses intending divorce actually effects talaq. The key lies in what talaq is designed to remove: a restriction (qayd) that is exclusive to the wife. Understanding this principle will help you correctly judge commonly used phrases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two expressions and their rulings
The passage discusses two scenarios: 'ana minki taliq' (I am divorced from you) which does not effect talaq, and 'ana minki bain' (I am separate from you) or 'alayki haram' (you are forbidden to me) which do effect talaq if intended. Note the ruling for each.
2
Understand the underlying principle
Talaq removes al-qayd (the restriction) that marriage places on the wife. This restriction – e.g., prohibition to remarry, need for husband's permission to leave – is exclusively on her. Ibanah (separation) removes al-wusla (the connection) which is shared between both spouses. Similarly, tahrim (making forbidden) removes al-hill (permissibility) which is also shared.
3
Trace the proof (talil)
The author proves that qayd is on the wife alone by noting that she cannot marry others or leave without permission, while the husband can marry up to three others and enjoy his slaves. Therefore, talaq must be directed at the wife to remove her restriction; saying 'I am divorced' targets the husband's own supposed restriction, which does not exist.
4
Apply to other similar expressions
Consider expressions like 'you are forbidden to me' (alayki haram). It removes hilla (permissibility) which is shared, so it can be directed at either spouse. Thus, it effects talaq when intended. The same applies to 'I am separate from you' – ibanah removes the shared connection.
5
Note the practical consequence
The ruling means a husband must be careful with his wording. Saying 'I am divorced from you' – even with explicit intention – does not count as talaq. He must use language that addresses the wife's restriction or the shared bond, such as 'You are divorced' or 'I am separate from you.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الطَّلَاقَ لِإِزَالَةِ الْقَيْدِ بِخِلَافِ الْإِبَانَةِ فَإِنَّهَا لِإِزَالَةِ الْوُصْلَةِ. وَإِنْ قَالَ لِامْرَأَتِهِ أَنَا مِنْكِ طَالِقٌ فَلَيْسَ بِشَيْءٍ وَإِنْ نَوَى طَلَاقًا، لِأَنَّ الطَّلَاقَ لِإِزَالَةِ الْقَيْدِ، وَهُوَ فِيهَا دُونَهُ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّهَا هِيَ الْمَمْنُوعَةُ مِنْ التَّزَوُّجِ وَالْخُرُوجُ وَالزَّوْجُ يَنْطَلِقُ إِلَى مَا شَاءَ مِنْ التَّزويج بِثَلَاثٍ سِوَاهَا وَيَسْتَمْعُ بِإِمَائِهِ وَإِنْ قَالَ أَنَا مِنْكَ بَائِنْ أَوْ عَلَيْكِ حَرَامٌ يَنْوِي الطَّلَاقَ طَلَقَتْ ، لِأَنَّ الْإِبَانَةَ لِإِزَالَةِ الْوُصْلَةِ وَهيَ مُشْتَرَكَةٌ، وَكَذَا التَّحْرِيمُ لِإِزَالَةِ الْحِلِّ وَهُوَ مُشْتَرَى فَصَحْتُ إِضَافَتُهَا إِلَيْهِمَا.
Indeed, talaq is for the removal of the restriction, unlike ibanah, for it is for the removal of the connection. And if he says to his wife, 'I am divorced from you,' it is nothing, even if he intended talaq, because talaq is for removal of the restriction, and it is in her not in him. Do you not see that she is prohibited from marrying and leaving, while the husband may marry up to three others besides her and enjoys his slaves. And if he says, 'I am separate from you' or 'what is upon you is forbidden' intending talaq, she is divorced, because ibanah is for removal of the connection, and it is shared, and similarly tahrim is for removal of permissibility, and it is shared, so its addition to both is valid.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage from al-Hidayah explains a critical distinction in the wording of talaq. Talaq is defined as removing the qayd (restriction) that marriage places on the wife. This restriction includes her inability to remarry or leave the house without permission. This qayd resides only in the wife, not the husband. Therefore, if a man says 'ana minki taliq' (I am divorced from you), no talaq occurs because he is attempting to remove a restriction from himself, which is not the function of talaq. However, if he says 'ana minki ba'in' (I am separate from you) or 'alayki haram' (you are forbidden to me) with the intention of talaq, talaq does occur, because ibanah (separation) removes the wusla (connection) which is shared between both spouses, and tahrim (making forbidden) removes the hilla (permissibility) which is also shared. These expressions can be directed at either spouse because they concern a shared attribute.

Key Terms
القيد (al-qayd): The restriction imposed by marriage on the wife, such as the prohibition to remarry and the obligation of husband's permission to leave.
الوصلة (al-wusla): The marital connection or bond shared between husband and wife.
الإبانة (al-ibanah): Separation or disconnection, which removes the shared marital connection.
الحرام (al-haram): Forbidden; in this context, 'alayki haram' (you are forbidden to me) removes the permissibility (hill) of marital relations, which is shared.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because he intended talaq.
B) No, because talaq removes the restriction on the wife, not the husband.
C) Yes, if he says it three times.
D) No, because he did not say 'anti taliq'.

Key Takeaway
Talaq requires wording that removes the wife's restriction (qayd); 'I am divorced from you' fails because it targets the husband's non-existent restriction.

Effect of Doubt in Talaq: 'One or Nothing'
Explains effect of doubt in talaq wording with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule that no divorce occurs when a husband says 'Anti taliq wahidatan aw la', and differentiate this from Imam Muhammad's view.

Core Idea
Doubt in the number of divorces (adad) becomes doubt in the act of effectuation, preventing talaq.

When a husband says 'You are divorced one or nothing', a divorce may or may not occur depending on how the doubt is analyzed. The Hanafi school is divided: the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that no divorce occurs because the doubt expressed by 'aw la' enters the essence of the effectuation. Imam Muhammad, in one narration, holds that one divorce occurs because the doubt is only in the description of 'one'. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and shows you how to apply the principle that occurrence is by the number, not the description.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wording and the doubt
The husband says 'Anti taliq wahidatan aw la' (You are divorced one or nothing). The word 'aw' introduces a doubt between 'one' and 'nothing'. The question is whether this doubt prevents talaq from occurring.
This is different from 'Anti taliq aw la' (You are divorced or nothing), where doubt enters the very essence.
2
Understand Shaykhayn's argument
Shaykhayn argue that when a description (wasf) like 'taliq' is combined with a number (adad) like 'wahidah', the divorce occurs by the number, not the description. Therefore, doubt in the number becomes doubt in the act of effectuation itself, so no talaq occurs.
The principle: occurrence is by the number, not the description.
3
Understand Muhammad's argument
Imam Muhammad (in one narration) argues that the doubt is only in the description of 'one' because 'aw' separates it from the negation. The phrase 'anti taliq' remains certain, so one divorce occurs.
He treats 'anti taliq' as certain and 'wahidah' as doubtful, so the doubt does not affect the essence.
4
Apply the qiyas: non-consummated wife
Shaykhayn use an analogy: if a husband says to a non-consummated wife 'Anti taliq thalatha' (You are divorced three), three divorces occur. This proves that occurrence is by the number, not the description. If it were by description, she would become divorced by 'taliq' alone and 'thalatha' would be futile. Applying this to our case, doubt in the number (one or nothing) means doubt in effectuation, so no talaq.
This qiyas strengthens Shaykhayn's position and is cited as decisive by al-Marghinani.

اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی نہیں ہوتی لہذا مذکورہ صورت میں بھی طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی۔ اگر کوئی شخص أنت طالق واحدة يا ثلاثا “ کہے تو اس صورت میں وقوع طلاق وحدة “ یا ”ثلاثا " سے ہو گی ، وصف یعنی طالق" سے نہیں ہوگی ، اس کی واضح دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے غیر مدخول بیوی سے ”أنت طالق ثلاثا کہا، تو اس پر تین طلاق واقع ہو جائیں گی ، دیکھئے یہاں بھی وقوع کا تعلق وصف سے نہیں بلکہ عدد یعنی ”ثلاثا‘ سے ہے، اس لئے کہ اگر وقوع کا تعلق وصف یعنی طالق سے ہوتا تو اس صورت میں وہ عورت طالق “ سے ہی بائنہ ہو جاتی اور ثلاثا " کا ذکر لغو ہو جاتا ۔
لَوْ قَالَ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ وَاحِدَةً أَوْ لَا عِنْدَ الشَّيْخَيْنِ خِلَافًا لِمُحَمَّدٍ فِي رِوَايَةٍ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَبِي يُوسُفَ، أَوْ لَا وَهُوَ رِوَايَةُ الطَّلَاقِ مِنْ الْمَبْسُوطِ . وَفِي الْهِدَايَةِ وَلَوْ كَانَ الْمَذْكُورُ فِى الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ قَوْلَ الْكُلِّ فَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ رِوَايَتَانِ، لَهُ أَنَّهُ أَدْخَلَ الشَّكْ فِي الْوَاحِدَةِ لِدُخُولِ حَرْفِهِ بَيْنَهُمَا وَبَيْنَ النَّفْي فَيَسْقُطُ اعْتِبَارُ الْوَحْدَةِ لِلشَّكِّ وَيَبْقَى قَوْلُهُ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ سَالِمًا عَنْ الشَّكْ بِخِلَافِ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ، أَوْ لَا لِأَنَّهُ أَدْخَلَ الشَّكْ فِي أَصْلِ الْإِيقَاعِ فَلَا يَقَعُ، وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ الْوَصْفَ مَتَى قُرِنَ بِالْعَدَدِ كَانَ الْوُقُوعُ بِذِكْرِ الْعَدَدِ لَا بِالْوَصْفِ فَكَانَ الشَّكُ دَاخِلا فِى الْإِيقَاعِ فَلا يَقَعُ وَلِهَذَا لَوْ قَالَ لِغَيْرِ الْمَدْخُولِ بِهَا أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ ثَلَاثًا وَقَعْنَ، وَلَوْ كَانَ الْوُقُوعُ بِالْوَصْفِ لَمَا وَقَعْنَ لِكَوْنِهَا أَجْنَبِيَّةً. مجمع الأنهر كاب الطلاق، فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان ، ج ۱ ص ۳۹۶، ط: دار إحياء التراث العربي الهداية كاب الطلاق، فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان ، ج ۲ ص ۳۸۵، ط: رحمانیه
Usool-e-Hidayah Volume Two: It does not occur, therefore in the mentioned case also divorce will not occur. If someone says 'You are divorced one or three', then divorce occurs from 'one' or 'three', not from the description 'divorced'. The clear proof is that if someone said to a non-consummated wife 'You are divorced three', three divorces occur. Notice here too occurrence is related to the number, not the description, because if occurrence were related to the description, she would become irrevocably divorced from 'divorced' alone, and mentioning 'three' would be futile. If he said 'You are divorced one or nothing': according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad in one narration, and it is the saying of Abu Yusuf, or 'nothing', and it is the narration of divorce from al-Mabsut. In al-Hidayah: if it was mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir as the saying of all, then from Muhammad there are two narrations. His argument is that he placed doubt in the 'one' because the letter 'or' enters between them and negation, so consideration of the unit falls due to doubt, and his statement 'You are divorced' remains free from doubt, unlike 'You are divorced or nothing' because he placed doubt in the essence of the effectuation, so it does not occur. Their (the two shaykhs') argument is that when the description is combined with the number, occurrence is by mention of the number, not the description, so doubt enters into the effectuation, therefore it does not occur. For this reason, if he said to a non-consummated woman 'You are divorced three', they occur, and if occurrence were by description, they would not occur because she is a stranger.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of doubt (shakk) in talaq wording. The issue is when a husband says to his wife 'Anti taliq wahidatan aw la' (You are divorced one or nothing). According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), no divorce occurs because the doubt (expressed by 'aw') enters into the very act of effectuation (asl al-iqa'). The doubt renders the intention uncertain, so talaq cannot be established. Imam Muhammad, in one narration, holds that one divorce occurs because the doubt is only in the description (wasf) of 'one', not in the essence of talaq. The passage uses qiyas to a non-consummated wife: if the husband says 'Anti taliq thalatha', three divorces occur, proving that occurrence is by the number, not the description. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the two shaykhs.

Key Terms
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt in the wording of talaq that prevents the intended divorce from occurring.
الوصف (al-wasf): The description 'taliq' (divorced) applied to the wife.
العدد (al-adad): The number of divorces (e.g., one, three) that actually effectuates the talaq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling when a husband says 'Anti taliq wahidatan aw la'?
A) One divorce occurs.
B) No divorce occurs.
C) Three divorces occur.
D) The wife becomes irrevocably divorced (ba'in) immediately.

Key Takeaway
Doubt in the number of divorces (adad) renders the entire effectuation doubtful, so no talaq occurs according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.
